The Grain and River-Bottom Rice Market Is Quiet 115

Zhabei: Yesterday, no boats arrived at the port via the waterway, and transactions in this street were even more scarce. The North Japonica rice from factories and warehouses has been registered by the authorities, but an agreement on evaluation and sale per peck has not been reached by both parties, making it difficult to proceed with the evaluation. The sales of Xiang rice and other varieties are completely sluggish. Although there is still a small amount of stock at the river bottom, there is little trading due to a lack of buyers. The wholesale price for top-quality rice is between 20.05 and 20.06 yuan, and the trend of converting to yuan is weak, with all sales being sluggish. There were a few sales per peck throughout the day at a high price of 19.78 yuan.

Hunan in Shanghai: There were few arrivals from the river bottom, and the buying interest in this street was very weak. North Japonica rice was extremely scarce, and the price was limited to a high of 21 yuan. Small amounts of thin Southern Indica rice were also being sold as needed. After the price of foreign rice rose firmly, the trend of Xiang rice became slightly more active, with the price settling at around 20 yuan. While conversion was not strong, reports from the waterways were calm, leading to a lack of interest from restaurants and taverns. The market sentiment was weak, but the price here still needs to be around 19 yuan. The sales of Yin yuan (silver dollars) were dull and sluggish.

Foreign Rice Drops Back by a Few Cents in the Afternoon 116

Yesterday morning, the price of foreign rice initially rose by four or five cents due to the jump in prices of various types of rice the day before, creating optimism. However, the previous rise after the fall was due to local merchants who found the small price increase worthwhile and made some inquiries. Furthermore, with the complete arrival of foreign rice orders, sentiment inevitably increased, and prices rose. However, traders from Huai'an again felt the price was too high and adopted a wait-and-see attitude. Many speculators, seeing a chance to profit, rushed to sell off their inventories, and the market could not sustain the gains for long. In the afternoon, the price fell by about one cent. Total transactions were also weak, only around 5,000 bags. There were over 4,000 bags of brown rice, priced at 16.75 to 16.5 yuan for small sizes, 16.95 yuan for extra-high quality, 15.3 to 15.4 yuan for large sizes, 14.78 yuan for red large sizes, 17.35 yuan for Kagai rice, 14.9 yuan for Min dang brown rice, and 14.1 to 13.9 yuan for small-sized brown rice from Qieladi, it is said.

The Flour Market Increased Again Yesterday 117

The Exchange Suspended Afternoon Trading Due to the Hot Weather

Yesterday morning, the flour market initially remained weak and sluggish. Subsequently, the price of foreign wheat was reported to be slightly better, and sentiment turned upward. Although actual sales were not brisk at the moment, factory inventories had not been sufficiently replenished due to the difficulty in purchasing wheat. Although the bulls, both internal and external, wanted to maintain high prices, they ultimately felt that the actual situation was not favorable, so they had to gradually cover their positions. As a result, prices for all near-term months increased. Long-term prices were relatively stable. Observing this, if sales do not improve, there should be no problems for this month; otherwise, a slight increase may be necessary. As a result, this month's price increased by 1.75 cents compared to the end of the previous week. Prices for August and September each increased by 1.5 cents, October increased by 1.25 cents, November increased by 1 cent, and December increased by 0.25 cents.

The flour exchange has temporarily suspended afternoon trading for one week due to the extreme heat. The trading sessions have been increased to six in the morning. Future arrangements will be determined based on the weather conditions.

Futures Wheat Rises and Then Retreats 118

Yesterday, the futures wheat market initially showed signs of rebounding in all months after the morning opening. This was due to the slight improvement in the price of foreign wheat and the sharp decline at the end of the previous week, which greatly stimulated speculation. As a result, prices in all months rose gradually, generally recovering by about four or five cents compared to the end of the previous week. However, when trading resumed in the afternoon, many large domestic bull traders took advantage of the tense sentiment to sell off their positions. The most active selling came from the Wuxi group. Factories also put slight pressure on the market. As a result, sentiment turned weak, retreating by two or three cents compared to the morning. In the end, July and September were each up by two cents, August, November, and December were up by one cent, and October was up by three cents. The spot wheat market was generally rejecting each other, intentionally suppressing prices, and unwilling to allocate high prices due to poor flour sales. As a result, prices in all segments were slightly sluggish. For example, Henan stale wheat has opened low at five taels. More than 3,000 bags of new wheat, such as those from Yaowan, Zhumadian, Shashi, and Hankou, were handled by Fuxin, it is said.

Subsequently, trading became more active, and spot sales remained acceptable, so the closing price recovered by about one cent. As a result, it was similar to the end of the previous week.

Local News

Typhoon in This Port Yesterday 126

Since entering the summer, the weather in this port has been hot, with thermometers often exceeding 90 degrees. However, the day before yesterday evening, the clouds in the sky moved very quickly, and a cool breeze gradually rose in the evening, mixed with light rain, suggesting signs of a typhoon. The summer heat dissipated as a result. Yesterday morning, a strong wind blew, with incessant whistling sounds. The tide in the Huangpu River rose sharply by several feet. The Customs flag station in Lujiazui, Pudong, received a report from the observatory stating that the typhoon was approaching rapidly from the Wenzhou waters in a northwesterly direction, appearing to be heading towards Shanghai. Therefore, at 10 a.m., it hoisted a black warning ball and simultaneously fired a warning shot to warn all shipping companies in this port that exports should temporarily stop anchoring to avoid danger. As a result, all shipping companies' exports were temporarily blocked yesterday. According to a report from the Xujiahui Observatory at 4 p.m. yesterday, the typhoon had landed in the Wenzhou area and turned north, now located at latitude 29 degrees and longitude 120 degrees, i.e., between Wenzhou and Ningbo. Its center point is about 30 li in length and width and is moving very quickly. If the wind direction does not change, it will pass several tens of li west of Shanghai. If it tilts slightly eastward, Shanghai will bear the brunt, it is said.

Fortunately, there were no accidents involving ships on the river surface due to the Customs' warning. Many buildings on land and residents' glass windows were shattered. The roof of the baseball viewing platform in the racecourse was also blown away in one corner. Many trees on both sides of the roads in western Shanghai were broken. It was truly a rare typhoon this year.

The Seawall in Baoshan Is in Danger 127

Please Allocate a Large Sum of Money Quickly for Emergency Repairs

The entire seawall in Baoshan County, northeast of the Wusong Fort and Taiwan, is related to the lives and property of the counties of Shanghai, Baoshan, Jiading, and Taicang. In recent days, sudden typhoons have occurred outside the Wusongkou, and the sea tide has risen sharply, accompanied by turbulent waves and towering white waves. As a result, the embankments along the east-west sides of the seawall have been washed away by the raging tide for about several hundred zhang. Wang Yizhong, the director of the Jiangnan Embankment Engineering Office, upon hearing this, immediately went to the seawall with several engineers to conduct an on-site inspection. The number of dangerous sections and the required engineering costs are detailed below: (1) The entire section of dangerous works from Wuyuedun, Pilian, and Beiwang Temple in Xitang is 276 zhang long. Among them, the foundation of 135 zhang of the embankment has collapsed, the embankment has been eroded, and only four or five feet of the embankment surface remain. It is in danger of collapsing and requires an estimated cost of over 97,000 yuan. (2) The east and west wing walls of the seawall connected to both ends of the Shidong Bridge are 1 zhang and 1 chi high. The east wing is 1 zhang and 4 chi long, and the west wing is 1 zhang and 7 chi long, with a total estimated cost of 2,500 yuan. (3) The foundation stones on the north and south sides of the outer mouth of the Shidong Bridge have all collapsed, with a length of about 15 zhang. It is the most important thing to protect Shidong and requires an estimated cost of 8,000 yuan. (4) Restoring all the foundation stone earthwork will require an estimated cost of over 39,000 yuan. The most dangerous sections that urgently need emergency repairs require a total estimated cost of over 140,000 yuan for labor, materials, etc. Director Wang has already submitted a detailed report on the dangerous situation of the embankment and the required funds to the Construction Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, requesting the immediate allocation of funds for emergency repairs to strengthen the embankment and prevent collapse.

All Sea Vessels Were Suspended Yesterday Due to the Typhoon 128

Yesterday, a typhoon occurred in this port, and coastal merchant ships were all blocked from leaving. The suspension of each route and the accidents of merchant ships are recorded as follows:

Ningbo Ships Suspended: The Shanghai-Ningbo scheduled ships Taikoo and Ningshao were suspended once during the big wind that occurred last Monday when the Xin Beijing and Xin Ningshao ships were suspended once. Until yesterday, after the two ships came to Shanghai from Ningbo and unloaded their cargo and passengers, they received a notice from the Jianghai Customs stating that a typhoon had occurred in this port. The wind in the Wenzhou waters was the strongest. Coastal merchant ships should stop exporting and take shelter in the port to show seriousness. Taikoo Ningshao immediately ordered Xin Beijing and Xin Ningshao to stay in Shanghai and stop leaving, stop loading cargo, and stop selling passenger tickets. More than a thousand passengers who arrived at the ship temporarily returned.

Zhejiang Sea Ships Stop: Zhoushan ship on the Shanghai-Taiwan line and Shengli ship on the Xiangshan line were all scheduled to depart from Shanghai before 5 p.m. yesterday. According to the usual practice, the time limit must not be wrong. Yesterday afternoon, the cargo and passengers of each ship had boarded the ship and waited for export. Because the Customs issued a warning, each ship did not dare to drive rashly and planned to move to the Wusongkou anchorage and wait for departure when the wind subsided slightly in the evening. In addition, the Zhaoshang Bureau's Hai'an ship also took shelter from the wind and repaired the wireless equipment on the ship. It was changed to export today.

Two Foreign Ships Aground: The Yifeng ship of the Yichang class of the Jiang Company in this port, which came to Shanghai from the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, imported yesterday. When the ship arrived at the Huangpu River and reached the river surface at the Bund of the Waibaidu Bridge, it happened to be the time when the wind and waves in the Huangpu River were large. The ship's hull was unable to control itself due to the impact of the waves and ran aground in front of the Bund Garden. A barge was also crushed. The company received the news and quickly sent a small ship to tow it. After more than two hours, it was towed out of the shoal. In addition, the Zhagen ship of the Zhawa Company in this port received a telegram. The company's Zhigen ship was on its way from Shanghai to Dalian and ran aground outside Dalian Bay due to a big wind. It is now sending a ship to rescue it.

Ships Coming to Shanghai Take Shelter from the Wind: In addition to the Luoyang Maru and Xianghe ships from the Yangtze River, most of the ships coming to Shanghai from the outer sea failed to arrive at the port and anchored outside Wusong to take shelter from the wind, such as the British ship Sha Bi Ding and the German ship Gu Sila. All took shelter from the wind on the way. In addition, the Zhaoshang Bureau's Jiahe ship came from Min to Shanghai and is currently sailing to Fuyang Island to take shelter from the wind. The Guangli ship came to Shanghai from Guangdong, carrying 1,000 unarmed soldiers, and was originally scheduled to land at Nangaogang Temple in Shanghai today. Yesterday, due to the typhoon on the way, it took shelter from the wind in Ningbo and did not leave. There are more than a dozen other ships that were blocked on various islands and failed to reach Shanghai, it is said.

Sampans Also Stopped: The small sampan boats in the river carried many passengers to and from. After receiving the big wind warning yesterday, they all sailed to various river branches and wharf berths in advance and stopped. The cargo barges did not leave due to the suspension of the sea ships and the huge wind and waves in the Huangpu River. All Jianglun loading and unloading of goods were changed to large iron barges to transport them carefully. From the afternoon of yesterday, the barges, sampans, and small steamers sailing in the Huangpu River were almost completely suspended. In this turbulent wave, a port famine appeared. This is truly a rare event in Shanghai, and most of the towed barges, small steamers, and civilian ships that were suspended sailed to the Suzhou River to take shelter from the wind.

French Celebrate Democracy Memorial Yesterday 129

French Overseas Chinese Hold Celebration

Yesterday was the anniversary of the French Democratic Republic. In the early morning, the French Consul-General, Mr. Gan Gelin, and the French military commander in Shanghai went to Gujiazhai Park to hold a military parade. At 8 o'clock, Mr. Fei Woli, the Police Superintendent of the French Concession Police, led the Chief Inspector, Mr. Pu Yan, and the heads and deputy heads of various police stations, and Chinese and Western detectives on duty, to the French Consulate on the Bund to congratulate Mr. Gan Gelin, the French Consul-General. They waited in the square in front of the consulate for the French Consul to hold a flag-raising ceremony. At 11 o'clock, they received congratulations in the main reception room of the French Consulate. The consuls of various countries stationed in Shanghai, such as Britain, the United States, and Japan, and the representatives of various Chinese military and political organs, etc., the judges of the French Public Concession, Zhu Gongtang, and Mr. Du Yuesheng, the Chinese consultant of the French Consulate, the Chinese director of the Ministry of Industry, the members of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, and the French Concession taxpayers' association, were all present. Mr. Gan Gelin, the French Consul-General, Mr. Ju Lan, the Zheng Consul, Mr. Zhang Wenbin, the translator, and Mr. Yin Yin warmly received them with champagne and refreshments. At 12 o'clock, they shook hands and said goodbye with great interest. At that time, the roads outside the consulate and the Bund were busy with traffic, which was very prosperous for a while. However, the French Park celebration and entertainment in the evening were stopped due to fears that a typhoon would occur and cause danger. The various kinds of news heard yesterday are compiled as follows:

Prisoner Relief: The French Concession Court has a tradition of prisoner relief every French Democracy Memorial Day. On the day before yesterday, the judge Zhu, together with Mr. Ju Lan, the French consul, drove to the prison on Xuehuali Road to ascend to the public seat. The prison head presented the list of prisoners to the case, which was reviewed by the Chinese and Western officials, and thirty-six prisoners who obeyed the law and worked diligently were selected for release, and the sentences of thirty-three prisoners were reduced to show compassion. The prisoners kowtowed and thanked them before leaving.

Suspension of Trial: The French Concession Court suspended the hearing of criminal cases in the morning and the civil court sessions in the afternoon due to the French National Day. According to the usual practice, the Chinese and Western officials notified the Criminal Section of the French Police Department and the Public Hall Prosecutor's Office to suspend the transfer of civil and criminal trivial cases for one day, and hung Chinese and French flags on the front door of the office to extend congratulations together.

Promotion: Mr. Fei Woli, the Police Superintendent of the French Police Department, specially promoted Du Wenbin, Cheng Haitao, and Yang Shansong, the translators of the Political Department, by one grade in commemoration of the country's democracy. Bao Tan, Fan Guangzhen, Wei Yuansheng, and Wang Danting were also promoted by one grade. In addition, Bao Tan, Zhu Liangbi, was specially promoted to Deputy Detective because of his outstanding work performance to encourage him.

French Water and Electricity Factory Damaged Underground Water Pipes Yesterday 130

It Is Said That It Will Take Tonight to Repair

At about 1:35 a.m. yesterday, the French water and electricity factory's water pipes at three locations, namely, the west end of Bansongyuan Road and Lujiabang Pubei Road in Nanshi, and in front of the water company's gate, suddenly burst at the same time, with the explosion at Bansongyuan being the most violent. It is estimated that a water pipe with a diameter of 12 inches and a length of about 12 feet was destroyed, and the road was destroyed for about 10 feet. Suddenly, the ground was flooded to a depth of one foot, and the shops and residences in the nearby area were turned into a swamp. The Second District General Office immediately sent a telegram to the General Office to notify the company. At dawn, the company sent a Western engineer and eight Russian workers, accompanied by Gao Xun, an official of the Second District, with many police officers, to investigate. Fortunately, there were a total of three main water pipes in the area. They immediately closed the main faucet of the damaged pipe and thoroughly investigated the cause of the damage. Therefore, the Chinese trams from Laoximen to Gaochang Temple could only drive to the Local Court and turn around. The trams running from Xiaodongmen to Gaochang Temple could only reach Xuejiabang. Until 10 a.m., after the water had completely receded, it was restored. According to the engineer, it would take at least tonight to repair. As for the other two locations, there was no major problem, it is said.

News of the Labor Unrest at the French Water and Electricity Factory Yesterday 131

Xiao Zhengfa, a worker at the French water and electricity workers' union, was injured in the wrist by a Westerner from the company for preventing new workers from repairing water pipes. He was taken to the Public Security Bureau by the Second District Police Station for questioning. The labor union immediately requested the Municipal Party Department to approve his release on bail so that he could receive treatment. The circumstances have been recorded in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that although Xiao was granted permission by the Public Security Bureau to be released after a brief interrogation, he was sent to court again at 8 a.m. yesterday. The labor union, upon hearing this, immediately dispatched four representatives, Zhu Xingeng, Jiang Ayou, Zhang Amao, and Xu Changgen, to report to the Municipal Party Department at 10 a.m. After Tao Baichuan received them, he immediately sent Mao Tongsheng to the Local Court to negotiate. As a result, they agreed to release him on bail. The labor union will go to bail him out this morning. Yesterday, the Public Security Bureau sent armed police officers to protect the company to repair water pipes. The workers were greatly angered upon hearing this, thinking that since the Chinese officials recognized that the French merchants had not registered with the Chinese authorities, there was no need to protect them. Furthermore, they have repeatedly maintained the French merchants in repairing the water pipes. When will the victory of the strike be achieved? Therefore, they specially convened a temporary discussion meeting and will go to the Municipal Party Department at 9 a.m. today to petition, state everything, and request relief.

Over Sixty Labor Unions Jointly Petition to Organize a Support Association for the Strike by Workers of the French Water and Electricity Factory. The Xiangsheng Iron Factory Workers' Union is not only making every effort to help but also raising donations to subsidize them. It is heard that they have already raised fifty silver dollars and handed them over to the water and electricity workers' union. The remaining funds will continue to be raised. The striking workers were very grateful for the enthusiasm of the Xiangsheng Workers' Union, it is said.

Xu Jiqing Resigns from Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Chairmanship 133

Reply to a Letter from Over Forty Trade Associations in the City

Mr. Xu Jiqing, the new chairman of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, replied yesterday to a letter from over forty trade associations in the city, stating his reasons for resigning. His original letter stated: "To the esteemed gentlemen of the Shanghai National Medicine Trade Association and forty other associations, I respectfully reply: Having read the reports in the city's newspapers of the 14th regarding your letter to me, Xu Jiqing, with earnest expectations and deep admonitions, I am filled with trepidation. My refusal to assume the chairmanship of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce is not, as your esteemed letter suggests, a feigned modesty for high praise. I stated on the spot that I would still serve as a committee member, hoping to follow the other committee members and contribute to some extent. However, I believe I am not capable enough to hold the chairmanship, fearing that my limited abilities would lead to inadequacy in the future. As for your esteemed letter stating that I would fail to live up to the expectations of all the merchants in the city, I feel even more guilty. Therefore, despite the repeated and sincere encouragement from the supervisors and committee members, my intention to yield the position to someone more capable remains unchanged. I sincerely hope that your esteemed associations will understand and forgive me. Your esteemed associations are concerned about the stagnation of chamber affairs, which I also deeply regret. I have already formally submitted a letter to the chamber, fully expressing my thoughts and requesting a re-election. This matter concerns the common interests of all merchants in the city, and I am sure it will be approved. I offer this reply with respect and wish you all good fortune. Xu Jiqing."

Compensation for Casualties at the Military Factory on June 3rd 135

Paid Out Yesterday

Compensation for the families of the victims of the June 3rd incident at the Military Factory was distributed yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM at the factory's guard battalion. Members of the aftermath committee, Ding Shuhui, and labor union representative Du Jinbang supervised the distribution. For each of the twenty-two deceased, the factory provided a compensation of 300 yuan, and employees donated 335.87 yuan. For the deceased engineer Shi Changhua, the factory provided a compensation of 1,100 yuan, and employees donated 335.97 yuan. For the three seriously injured, each received a compensation of 50 yuan from the factory and 150 yuan from employee donations. For the ten slightly injured, one received 30 yuan from the factory and 60 yuan from employee donations, two received 30 yuan from the factory and 30 yuan from employee donations, and seven received 30 yuan from the factory and 15 yuan from employee donations. Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Encourages Purchase of Indica Rice and Flour 140

Another Solution to Relieve the City's Food Shortage

To implement the policy of relieving the city's food shortage, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has recently issued a

Page 14

public notice encouraging citizens to purchase indica rice and flour to prevent unscrupulous merchants from hoarding and raising prices. The original text is as follows: "Public Notice: Recently, rice prices have soared, making it difficult for people to obtain food. This bureau has carefully considered the commercial situation and people's livelihood and has set a maximum price for high-quality white japonica rice in the market not exceeding 21 yuan. The price of medium-quality rice should be reduced accordingly, and it is forbidden to sell medium-quality rice at high prices. Furthermore, the price of rice ships arriving in Shanghai will be publicly assessed and distributed to rice shops for sale. This is all to eliminate under-the-table pricing and allow rice shops to sell at correct prices, ensuring that both large and small rice shops have fair access to rice and that citizens can enjoy the benefits of price limits. However, it has recently been reported that some rice shops are still selling white japonica rice at prices as high as 23 or 24 yuan. This bureau has sent personnel to investigate and found that rice shops are generally complying with the price limits. Therefore, the accuracy of the reported news remains to be verified. However, we hope that citizens will follow the bureau's Public Notice No. 154. If any rice shop is found to be charging prices higher than the price limit or selling medium-quality rice at high prices, citizens should immediately submit the receipt or a sample of the rice to the bureau, and strict punishment will be imposed. If citizens do not report such violations and rely solely on the limited number of personnel in this bureau to supervise the thousands of rice shops in the city, it will be impossible to achieve the goal. Therefore, the government's orders can only be implemented with the assistance of the citizens. Citizens, you must know that the rice is currently in the hands of hoarders and large rice merchants. It is not that there is no rice, but that it is not in the hands of farmers. The hoarders believe that the higher the market price, the less willing they will be to sell. They are using the name of the poor autumn harvest last year to fulfill their dreams of getting rich. They do not care about the people's livelihood or consider the people's interests. If you want to buy their rice, they will hoard it and demand high prices. A few rice shops have the same mentality. If we can refrain from buying japonica rice, they will lose the opportunity to hoard. If they cannot sell it in the future, they will be willing to lower the price themselves. Moreover, this bureau has carefully tested various types of white japonica rice and found that the so-called 'special' or 'top-grade' white japonica rice is the least nutritious. You are paying high prices for unhealthy rice, and what you are buying is indica rice. That is the most unprofitable. You did not understand this before, so you bought it. Now that you know, you should realize this and stop buying that expensive and useless top-grade white japonica rice. According to rice merchants, the harvest in various regions this year is expected to be abundant. The abundant harvest of indica rice in Anhui and Jiangxi can be confirmed. The new japonica rice in Kunshan and Zhoupu will be available in half a month at the earliest and in a month at the latest. The peak season will last for little more than a month. There will no longer be the same panic as in the past. When the new rice is available, the hoarders will also release their rice. Furthermore, there are still 800,000 to 900,000 bags of indica rice in the city's warehouses, which is enough to feed the city's population. In the past, people from all over came to Shanghai to buy rice. Now that new wheat is available in the north, the need for rice has decreased. New rice is also available in the Yangtze River region. For example, Zhejiang Province, which has always lacked rice, is now reselling the indica rice it previously bought. Under these circumstances, even if hoarders do not sell a single stone of japonica rice and no rice boats come from the lower reaches of the river, the citizens of Shanghai will not have to worry about not having food. Therefore, this bureau hopes that citizens will not be confused by the atmosphere created by the hoarders and large rice merchants and give them the opportunity to profit. At this time of japonica rice shortage, since there is a large supply of indica rice, we should immediately start eating indica rice or switch to flour. Flour is not lacking in nutrients and is also a domestic product, which is beneficial to people's livelihood and the economy, especially worth buying. This bureau has the responsibility to regulate the food supply and will do its best to do so. Therefore, this public notice is issued to citizens, calling for concerted efforts to switch to indica rice and flour. This is of utmost importance. Special Announcement." (Wuchen News Agency)

Department of Agriculture and Mining Sends Personnel to Purchase Bovine Plague Serum 144

▲ Commodity Inspection Bureau Sends Personnel to Towns for Inoculation

Previously, the Livestock and Product Inspection Office of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau had successfully produced bovine plague serum. As a trial, they voluntarily inoculated cattle near Shanghai affected by bovine plague to test the serum and gradually spread it to various regions. Recently, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture and Mining, due to the outbreak of bovine plague in the Fourth District of Zhenjiang, planned to purchase bovine plague serum from the bureau to prevent its spread and requested that personnel be dispatched to the district to carry out inoculations. The department specially sent Zhang Zhenlin, a member of the Agricultural Extension Committee, to Shanghai to discuss the matter. The department requested that the serum be provided at half price. It is now learned that the bureau has sent technician Shou Biao, accompanied by Committee Member Zhang, carrying a large batch of serum to various rural villages to inoculate draft cattle and strive for relief.

Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Weaving Associations Telegraph Request to Amend Factory Regulations 145

The Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Weaving Associations telegraphed the National Government, Executive Yuan, Legislative Yuan, and Ministry of Industry and Commerce yesterday, stating (excerpt): "We have recently received a letter from the Suzhou Iron Silk Weaving Association and others stating that the scale and equipment required by the Factory Law are so vast and detailed that only large factories with huge capital can afford them. Today, Article 1 of the General Provisions (this law applies to those employing 30 or more workers), etc., states that small factories employing 30 or more workers cannot afford such large-scale equipment. Even small factories with hundreds of workers do not have such great financial resources. If this is implemented, not only will there be no effect, but it will inevitably lead to labor unrest and increasingly serious disputes. In recent years, the situation has been turbulent, and labor unrest has occurred frequently. Losses have been frequent, and factories have been struggling. How can they afford the burden of this law? Furthermore, the disputes will become more severe, and there will be more unemployment. Everyone views setting up a factory as a dangerous path, which is not the original intention of the legislation. According to the facts, it is necessary to revise it again. Before the date of implementation is announced and the implementing rules are drafted, we propose that you promptly deliberate and forward this to the relevant authorities for consideration. Accordingly, this matter was specially submitted to the Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Industry Emergency Conference on June 22nd for public discussion. After deliberation by all representatives, it was unanimously resolved to request the National Government to amend the (30 workers) in Article 1 (this law applies to those employing 30 or more workers) to (3,000 workers) so that commercial sentiment and legal intent can be balanced, and the difficulties of small industrial factories at present can be relieved. Respectfully telegraphing this request in accordance with the decision, earnestly requesting a prompt proposal to the General Assembly for a resolution to amend, announce, and implement." Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Weaving Associations.

Ham Industry Opposes Additional Taxes in Zhejiang Province (Continued) 147

The ham tax in Zhejiang Province has been consistently nine cents per ham. Starting June 1st this year, the Zhejiang Department of Finance suddenly announced a tax of sixteen cents per ham, causing opposition from ham merchants in various places. The Shanghai Ham Industry Association had previously petitioned the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to forward the matter to the Zhejiang Provincial Government, requesting a cancellation. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce has now received a reply from the Zhejiang Provincial Government. It reads as follows: "To the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce: Having received the cablegram from you, we have investigated the matter of additional taxes on ham in this province. Previously, representatives of the ham industry in the five counties of Jinhua, including He Shaohan, as well as the cocoon, Dongyang, and Yiwu county chambers of commerce and ham merchants, repeatedly telegraphed requesting exemption from the additional tax. The provincial government ordered the Department of Finance to review the matter. Subsequently, the department reported that ham is a semi-luxury item. The proposed increase in the tax rate should not exceed 5%, and the burden will still be transferred to the consumers. This should not affect ham merchants or agriculture. The request should not be considered. The department has instructed the county governments to inform them. This case is specially recorded and replied to, hoping to inform the relevant parties." After receiving this reply, the ham industry unanimously believes that the Zhejiang Department of Finance's designation of ham as a semi-luxury item is unfounded. If ham can be called a luxury item, then what about silk and other similar products? The proposed increase in the tax rate should not exceed 5%, which is clearly a result of inaccurate investigation. Various reasons are being prepared to jointly petition the central government with ham industries from various places to achieve the goal of cancellation.

Employees of Two Railways Petition Liu Weichi 148

▲ Liu Expresses Full Acceptance

Employees of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, due to the Railway Department's newly promulgated salary increase regulations being more restrictive than the old regulations, sent twelve representatives from the five major sections of the railway, including Traffic, Mechanical, Accounting, Engineering, and Electrical, to meet with Director Liu Weichi to petition him on behalf of all employees and to request Minister Sun to withdraw the order. This was reported in the previous issue. It is now learned that the representatives met with Director Liu at 10:00 AM that morning. The representatives first stated the employees' grievances, mainly stating that the salary increase regulations for the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways had been set long ago, and the employees had always worked diligently and had never complained. For example, two years ago, the Telegraph and Postal Bureaus requested salary increases due to the difficulty of living, but the employees of our two railways remained the same. The standard of living was lower than it is now, and their income was barely enough to make a living. However, in the past two years, prices have risen, and recently, gold prices have soared, increasing the cost of living by more than two or three times. The Postal and Telegraph Bureaus have devised proper measures to compensate their employees for their livelihood, allowing them to work with peace of mind. However, not only have the employees of our two railways not received any compensation, but new regulations have been promulgated that reduce the annual salary increase from six yuan to five yuan, and the salary of one hundred yuan, which could be obtained in nine years, is delayed to thirteen years. Given that the original salary was already insufficient, the implementation of the new regulations would be tantamount to rowing against the current, and the livelihood prospects of the employees of the two railways would be bleak. What our employees are asking for now is simply to cancel the new regulations and maintain the original regulations. This is also reasonable and does not have any blackmailing intent. Since Director Liu has taken office, he has been committed to creating benefits for the employees and promoting the development of the two railways. He should adopt our proposal. Director Liu then spoke, stating that he fully accepted what the representatives said and would forward it to Minister Sun, and would do his best to petition on behalf of the employees of the two railways. For those with salaries below one hundred yuan, measures should be taken to provide compensation first.

City Health Bureau's Progress in Epidemic Prevention Inoculations - Recent News 153

Since the City Health Bureau expanded epidemic prevention inoculations on May 1st, over 230,000 citizens have benefited from free vaccinations. To further facilitate free vaccinations for citizens, the bureau continues to send medical personnel to factories, organizations, and densely populated slum areas for free inoculations. Recently, two mobile vaccination vehicles have been deployed, one in Zhabei and one in Nanshi,巡迴交通衝繁路口及各菜塲 [They] tour busy intersections and various vegetable markets daily to provide vaccinations for citizens. Each vehicle vaccinates approximately 1,000 people per day on average. Additionally, personnel are stationed on the first and second ferries of the Public Works Bureau, providing free vaccinations. Each ferry vaccinates approximately 100 people per day on average. According to bureau personnel, citizens have been enthusiastically seeking vaccinations this year. The current number of medical personnel is still insufficient due to two factors: Firstly, the Health Bureau's epidemic prevention efforts have been ongoing for two years, resulting in considerable public trust. Secondly, this year, funding has been provided by the National Government, allowing for greater development in personnel and publicity, making vaccinations more accessible to citizens. If sufficient funds were available to establish four or five free clinics, it would greatly benefit citizens in terms of epidemic prevention and medical treatment, it is said.

Lawyers to Correct New Uniforms - Effective September 1st 154

▲Implemented Starting September 1st

The Shanghai Lawyers Association issued a notice yesterday to all members, stating: "Respectfully, upon receiving Order No. 4279 from the Jiangsu High Court, regarding the correction of the new lawyer uniform regulations by July 1st of this year, the attached drawings were found to be inconsistent with the drawings published in the January 12, 18th year of the Republic of China Judicial Gazette. It is deeply feared that members will purchase different styles separately, leading to further discrepancies. Therefore, the Association designated a clothing store to produce sample uniforms and made corrections back and forth until completion. It is extremely difficult to complete the production within the deadline. Furthermore, inquiries with the presidents of the Second Branch of the High Court and the Special District Local Court revealed that neither court has received orders to correct the uniforms within a specific timeframe. The court inspectors and clerks of both courts have no plans to correct the new uniforms by a specific date. This raises the question of whether members of this Association should continue to wear the old uniforms in the various courts in the concessions after July 1st. For these two reasons, a request for a two-month extension was telegraphed on June 22nd. Subsequently, Order No. 3691 from the Jiangsu High Court was received, stating that the Association's request for an extension until September 1st for implementing the correction of lawyer uniforms was difficult to approve, and that the style of the hat should be in accordance with the style published in the Judicial Gazette. At the same time, a letter was received from Chief Prosecutor Wang of the same court, stating that the Association's difficulties and reasons for being unable to complete the production in time had been discussed with Court President Lin of the High Court, who agreed that all lawyers could continue to wear their existing uniforms in court until August 31st of this year, but that the order must be complied with on September 1st. Upon receiving this, in addition to submitting it to the Jiangsu High Court and the Shanghai Local Court for filing, a corresponding letter is hereby sent to your members, stating that the old uniforms may still be worn in court until August 31st of this year, but that the new lawyer uniforms must be corrected and implemented on September 1st. Please take note and act accordingly."

Public Works Bureau Refuses to Inspect Prostitutes 155

▲Taxpayers Association Forwards Reply to City Health Bureau

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association previously received a letter from the Shanghai City Health Bureau requesting notification to the concession authorities to inspect prostitutes. Yesterday, a reply from the Public Works Bureau regarding this matter was received. The Association immediately forwarded a letter to the City Health Bureau, stating: "Respectfully, regarding the matter of inspecting prostitutes, a reply from the Public Works Bureau has been received, stating in a letter dated July 6th: 'Regarding the request to implement the inspection of prostitutes, the prostitute issue was carefully considered by a special committee in 1919. As a result, all licensed brothels were officially closed by this Bureau. As for the inspection, it effectively entails two methods: registration and examination. Implementing it would be tantamount to the official recognition of brothel operations. Furthermore, registration has little obvious effect on suppressing prostitution and preventing venereal diseases. As for medical examinations, countries that have implemented similar methods have all failed, as examinations must be conducted daily, which is practically impossible to achieve. To make it truly effective, it must be accompanied by isolation and treatment measures. Based on the above two reasons, countries generally do not implement any other suppression measures for prostitution other than providing adequate medical facilities, such as venereal disease hospitals. Such medical facilities are already readily available in Shanghai. A corresponding reply is hereby sent for your information. We hope you will take note and act accordingly.'"

Local News II

Over 500,000 Gold Bars Seized on Canadian Empress 161

Three boxes containing over 300 gold bars

Wrapped in thick paper and tightly bound with cloth

Authorities are strictly investigating the smuggling merchants

Since the soaring gold prices and plummeting silver prices, China, as a silver standard country, has been greatly affected both domestically and internationally. Prices have risen, the people's livelihood has declined, and the national economy is in danger of fundamental bankruptcy. The government authorities have carefully planned relief measures. It is generally agreed that it is difficult to immediately switch to the gold standard in practice due to various difficulties. In order to alleviate the immediate crisis, in addition to ordering all customs offices to uniformly use gold units to collect taxes on import and export goods, an order has recently been issued to strictly prohibit the export of gold and the import of raw silver, in order to remedy the situation to the greatest extent possible. After the prohibition order was issued, the effect has not yet been seen, but it is known that some evil merchants have disregarded the survival of the country and secretly exported gold for profit. According to a report from the 報載 [newspaper] yesterday, in the past month, the amount of yellow goods shipped from China to Japan has reached a staggering 4 million yuan. The source is said to be that some Chinese people in Shanghai bought and transported it to Japan via Manchuria. It can be seen that the various transportation methods of these people cannot be known by outsiders. However, this is only the number from Japan alone, and the amount transported to other countries is not included. Moreover, Shanghai is the main port for export, so the Jianghai Customs authorities are inspecting foreign ships more strictly than before when they leave the port. The Canadian Empress, a large ship of the Changxing Company's World Class, arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong on the 12th and left for Hong Kong the day before yesterday (the 13th). When the ship was about to leave the dock at the China Merchants North Wharf, the customs authorities had received a tip-off in advance that a large amount of gold bars was secretly being exported on the ship, so they specially dispatched a number of Chinese and foreign customs officers to board the ship and search it. On the spot, they found three boxes in the cabin full of yellow goods, totaling more than 300 gold bars of various sizes. The large ones weighed about 20 taels of gold, and the small ones weighed five, six, or ten taels, with a total value of more than 500,000 yuan. Each gold bar was wrapped in thick paper and then tightly bound with cloth. The way they transported the gold onto the ship was very ingenious. They wore a canvas vest with a number of pockets sewn on it, and hid the gold bars in the pockets. Each person could hide more than 20 catties of gold each time, which is about 30,000 yuan. Then, they boarded the ship and secretly hid the vest with gold in the box. Their actions were secretive and difficult for outsiders to detect. After the huge amount of gold was discovered, it was transferred to a small boat by customs officers and transported to the customs warehouse for temporary storage. The customs authorities considered this the first major case of smuggling a huge amount of gold for export and attached great importance to it. At the same time, government officials also sent people to the customs to inspect and study the method of smuggling. It is reported that the authorities are now strictly investigating the smuggling merchants who secretly transported the huge amount of gold for export in order to investigate and handle the matter thoroughly. On the one hand, the seized gold will be temporarily kept in the warehouse, and the head of the 水巡捕房 [water police station] will be ordered to supervise the detectives to guard it.

Xu Xuqin Twice Escaped Death 162

▲First Taking Sleeping Pills

▲Then Jumping into the Huangpu River

▲Rescued Both Times

▲Youth Should Strive

Xu Xuqin from Shangyu is 19 years old. His father, Xu Hongzhou, is currently working as an engineer on the railway in Zhangjiakou, Hebei. When Xu was 13 years old, he studied at a middle school in Beiping with his father for more than two years, but then abandoned his studies and loafed around until now. However, his desire to study has never been abandoned. In March of this year, his father ordered him to return to his hometown, and then sent letters repeatedly urging Xuqin to return north. However, Xu, eager to study, never expressed his consent. Recently, after repeated urging from his uncle, he took 40 yuan of travel expenses and came to Shanghai by train in order to take a boat back north. Unexpectedly, 20 yuan was stolen from him on the train. He arrived in Shanghai on the 4th of this month and first stayed at the Qichang Hotel on Simalu [4th Avenue] for eight days, and then changed to the Shanghai New Hotel at Daxin Street. Unexpectedly, Xu, feeling sad about his fate, suddenly had the thought of厌世 [being tired of the world]. That evening, the waiter of the hotel saw him writing letters several times, but they were all torn up. The waiter was very suspicious. The next morning, when the sun was high, Xu had not yet gotten up. The waiter called him from outside, but there was no response, so he tried to move the door panel and enter. He saw Xu lying on the bed, barely breathing. He saw two bottles of sleeping pills on the table, knowing that he had taken medicine to commit suicide. He immediately tried various methods and splashed cold water on his face to wake him up. Later, it was learned that Xu bought the two bottles of sleeping pills for one yuan. However, the medicine was not very potent and his life was saved. Unexpectedly, Xu's desire to commit suicide did not diminish at all. The night before, he wrote a farewell letter to his father at the hotel and put it on the table. Yesterday morning, he took a ferry to Pudong. At 9:00 a.m., he took a Taikoo Company快大 [fast big]輪船 [steamship] from the Huatong Pier in Pudong and sailed to the center of the river. Xu immediately jumped into the river in an attempt to end his life. Fortunately, he was rescued by a sailor on the ship and handed over to Chinese Constable No. 44 of the 水巡捕房 [water police station], who took him to the police station. Xu's mind was still not very clear and he still looked tired, probably due to the sleeping pills. The police chief interrogated him and learned the whole story, and took his suicide note from the hotel. He then sent Chinese Detective No. 3 Cheng Yongnian to send Xu to the Shaoxing Seven Counties Association on Qipu Road to be taken in, and sent him to the hospital for treatment. After his spirit returned to its original state, he was sent back to his home. Here is a copy of his farewell letter to his father:

Beloved father, since I sent you two letters on the seventh and eighth of last month, more than a month has passed and I have not received a reply. My heart is extremely anxious. I wonder if you, sir, are angry that I have not gone north and will not answer. The reason why I hesitated to come north at that time was because I secretly wanted to apply to the Labor University in the south, which is why I delayed. My humble intention is nothing more than to seek study and employment. My uncle had already agreed to let me enter the school to study after the summer vacation, but since you, sir, previously wrote in your letter that you wanted me to return, your intentions were so earnest that I did not dare to mention staying to him until now. Waiting for your letter to arrive, I was afraid that you, sir, had already lost heart, and because the weather will gradually become hot in the future, the journey will be inconvenient, so he arranged travel expenses for me and urged me to go north as soon as possible in order to fulfill my filial piety. When I came, he told me that if I entered the school to study after coming north, he could send me tuition fees. His intentions were so generous that I could not refuse any longer, so I set off from home a few days ago. It has been several days since I came to Shanghai. Staying in the hotel, I think about my decision every day. For the past few days, my mind has been confused and my heart is very painful. Looking forward to the future, I hesitate to move forward. Thinking that my studies have been delayed for several months since I came south, what face do I have to see my father in the north? Alas, if fate is like this, what joy is there in life? After thinking for several nights, I feel that in order to relieve the pain of my body and mind, there is no better way than to destroy this body. Now I have decided to do this. I think that I am inherently stupid and did not work hard in the past. Now that I am older, I have not achieved anything in terms of knowledge. I only have regrets. Even if I steal my life in the world, I will only be mediocre and unable to glorify my family, nor can I continue your ambitions. It is better to die. If I have consciousness after death, I can see my ancestors and mothers in the underground, is it not more joyful than苟生 [living aimlessly]? Only thinking about relying on you, sir, for half my life, now that I am dying once and for all, receiving the kindness of raising me for nineteen years, then my crime of being unfilial is truly as deep as heaven and earth, and I cannot excuse myself. When writing this letter, how can I not be heartbroken and tears fall like rain? You, sir, are in your prime and do not have to worry about having no son. You also have a strong faith in religion and can understand this matter. I hope that you, sir, will not bear grudges and think about me, so that the soul in the springs will increase its sins and uneasiness. I am grieving while writing this letter and do not want to write more, lest it increase your pain. I write this with tears and sincerely wish you, sir, progress in your morality and cherish your future. Unfilial son Xuqin's last words, July 12.

Bathhouse Patrons Found Not Guilty in Russian Detective's False Accusation of Theft 163

▲Allegations by the Russian Detective

▲Cannot Be Proven

Qulun, a Russian detective from the General Patrol Room No. 220, was bathing at the Jiangwan Road Public Swimming Pool on the afternoon of the 6th of this month. Wang Caiqi, a Pudong native bathing with him, mistakenly took his towel. Qulun accused Wang of theft and wanted to take him to the police station. Guan Bomian, a native of Anhui who was also bathing, came forward to mediate and was also implicated. The next day, they were escorted to the Special District Local Court. It was ordered that Guan be released on bail and Wang be detained for questioning. It has been reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng continued the hearing. The Chinese and foreign witnesses who appeared in court included Yang Jinpeng, the inspector of the swimming pool, Kana, a westerner and inspector of the Public Works Bureau's health department, and the Russian You Yunke Limali. The court repeatedly questioned both sides for a long time. Judge Feng then pronounced that Wang and Guan were both not guilty. The lawyer from the Patrol Room heard the verdict and requested that Guan Bomian's 500 yuan bail be temporarily retained during the appeal period. The judge approved it.

Zhou Abing Recounts His Kidnapping Experience 164

▲Kidnappers Torture Hostage

▲Gunshots Ring Out, Kidnappers Flee

▲Entire Village Suspected of Being Accomplices

▲Old Woman Lends Key for Release

Zhou Rentang's son, Zhou Abing, a resident of Zhoujiazhai Township in 北蔡東首 [North Cai East First] in Pudong, is engaged in the business of driving barges. He owns several barges that are used by the Modern Cleaning Bureau to transport manure. A few days ago, Abing led two crew members in a barge loaded with 16 tons of manure to the Liantang area near Songjiang to unload it. When the empty boat was returning and passing through the 馬瀝港浦面 [Mali Port Surface] at the junction of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, it was suddenly encountered by a pirate ship, and several pirates jumped on board and looted it. In addition to taking all the more than 40 yuan in silver hidden under the stove, Abing was kidnapped. It is now known that Abing was in the bandit's den for five or six days, and he escaped the night before last. He has now arrived in Shanghai and recounted in detail his experience in the bandit's den. According to him, (the following is Abing's account): On that day, he was escorted by the bandits to the small town of Shihutang, and then to an empty house in Zhaojiabang (i.e., Zhaojia Hall) and locked up. The place was a village with dozens of households. There was only a wooden bed in the empty house. In the evening, a small, stout man resembling the bandit leader (about thirty years old, wearing glasses on his nose) came to interrogate me. The bandit asked if the manure boat was self-owned. I said it was the Cleaning Bureau's boat, and I was only transporting manure on behalf of the bureau. The bandit asked how much property my family had. I said my family was very poor. The bandit said he didn't believe me, that I was very cunning. Since I had more than 40 yuan in silver hidden under the stove, and I only said I had 3 yuan, it was really hateful. Since I was here, I needed 5,000 yuan to be redeemed. How much could I pay? I said I really had no money. The bandit said if I had no money, I would be tortured. So, the bandits stripped off my 香雲紗 [fragrant cloud gauze] pants, tied my hands and feet with ropes in the opposite direction, and hung me up in the air to torture me. Then, one bandit stood on my back and squatted down several times. After a while, they put me down, locked my neck with a huge iron chain, and locked one end on the bed leg, and sent two bandits to guard me. The next day, they came to torture me again. Because I could not bear the pain, I agreed to pay 1,000 yuan. The bandits did not agree and added another 400 yuan. The bandits still did not agree. I was locked up for five days and nights. The afternoon before last, I suddenly heard two gunshots outside, and it was rumored that the police were coming to search for the kidnappers. At this point, the two bandits guarding me told me that I was not allowed to make a sound or escape. After saying that, they left. But I was still locked up. I thought there was no way to unlock the lock, and there was nothing to break the iron chain. I had no way, so I lit the mosquito net with a candle, intending to set fire to it. Unexpectedly, the house was empty and only the mosquito net was burned, but the house was not set on fire. Neighbors saw the smoke billowing in the house and came in to investigate. I begged them to release me, but they ignored me. At this point, I thought that there was no way to survive, so I might as well take my own life to end my life. So, I slammed my head against the huge stone in front of the bed. Fortunately, an old woman came forward to stop me and said that she was going to do good deeds and release me. So, she got the key from another place and unlocked the lock. I thanked the old woman and escaped from the bandit's den at night. I ran all night and swam across three rivers and canals, including the 馬瀝港 [Mali Port]. Fortunately, I was not drowned. The next morning, I thought to myself that I had no money, and the 香雲紗 [fragrant cloud gauze] shirt and pants I was wearing had been stripped off by the bandits and replaced with tattered cloth pants. Barefoot, I was lucky enough to meet a manure boat that I knew, and I borrowed one yuan. I went to Shihutang Station and took a train to Shanghai. All the villagers in the bandit's den seemed to be accomplices. Every afternoon, seven or eight people wearing the 保衛團 [security corps] uniform came to the village with the villagers to commit crimes. The stolen money and silver were divided equally. The bandits all carried box cannons, pistols, short guns,刺刀 [bayonets] and other weapons. The Zhaojia Hall area was a well-known bandit's den. That day, I don't know where the two gunshots came from, causing the two thieves who were guarding me to flee, so I was able to escape in the meantime, which was also a stroke of bad luck. I recall being tortured by the bandits twice in the bandit's den, and I still feel the pain.

Yesterday's Final Arguments in the Fang Estate Dispute Case 167

▲ Verdict to be announced on the 21st of this month

The late Fang Danchi, originally from Hubei and formerly an official in Jiangxi Province, left behind an estate. His son, Fang Dacan, alleged that his father's third concubine, Deng, and her father, Deng Guannan, conspired with Wang Shutang to steal the estate. The former Provisional Court ruled against the plaintiff, Fang Dacan, who appealed, engaging lawyer Zhan Jifeng. Yesterday morning, Chief Judge Du of the Jiangsu Higher Court's branch court, along with Judges Gao and Ye, held a hearing, questioning each party in detail. Fang Dacan testified that the family estate was managed by his father and had not been divided among his uncles. Deng, his third stepmother, took advantage of his father's illness to steal 美豐, 中南, 四明, and 明華 bank passbooks and 120 gold pounds and seventeen taels and five mace of gold leaf from an iron box. Because the account books were stolen at the same time, the exact amount of the deposits could not be determined, but it was estimated to be between 160,000 and 200,000. This was discovered on the fifth day after his father's death on the fourth day of the eighth month of last year. Only Deng was present in his father's sickroom, serving him medicine. She has now admitted to stealing the gold pounds and gold leaf and handing them over to her father, who then passed them on to Wang Shutang for safekeeping. Therefore, the bank passbooks must also have been stolen in collusion. Wang was a close friend of his father and often came to their house, etc. Deng Guannan testified that he came to Shanghai last April to stay with his son-in-law, Fang Danchi. After Danchi's death, Dacan wanted to search his daughter's room, so his daughter handed over eighty gold pounds and more than ten taels of gold leaf to him, asking him to entrust them to Wang Shutang for safekeeping. At the end of August, the deceased's brother, Fengchi, asked Wang for the gold pounds, etc. Wang then returned the items to his daughter. He knew nothing about the passbooks. Deng also testified that her family's property was managed by her husband and his brother, Hechi, and she did not know the exact amount. The eighty gold pounds and more than ten taels of gold leaf were given to her by her husband as compensation for her jewelry, as she had gold jewelry that she could not wear during her father-in-law's funeral. Her husband sold the jewelry, and last summer, he gave her the gold pounds and gold leaf. After her husband's death, his brother, Fengchi, and Dacan, both forced her to hand over the gold items. Because she already owned them, she ordered her father to take them to Wang Shutang's house and entrust them to Wang for safekeeping. Later, Wang was asked for them by Fengchi, so he returned them to her. However, she was eventually forced to hand over forty-four gold pounds and the remaining gold leaf, which she had already sold and spent. She also denied knowing anything about the passbooks. Wang Shutang also admitted to holding the gold items for Deng and said that after Danchi's death, he had, at the request of his family, mortgaged tobacco and purchased a coffin on their behalf. Because the family had no funds, he temporarily mortgaged the gold pounds to a coffin shop (Jufeng Timber Company). When the tobacco mortgage was completed, he redeemed the gold pounds with the money and returned them to Deng, etc. Then, the arguments began. Lawyer Zhan first stated that Deng was Danchi's favorite concubine and often opened the iron box and withdrew money on his behalf when he was ill, or signed checks on his behalf. How could she not know the amount of property? In short, the account books of Jufeng Timber Company and Wang Shutang's bills could not be trusted. Finally, he pointed out that Deng came to Shanghai last December and did not stay at her uncle's house but stayed at Wang Shutang's place. Later, she and Wang were apprehended together at the North Station Inn. Deng Guannan's coming to Shanghai was even more suspicious. When he left Hubei, he said he was going upstream, but then he suddenly came to Shanghai, which was even more suspicious. Because of all these things, the plaintiff believed that there was a conspiracy to steal, so he appealed, requesting punishment and the return of all the property. Next, the lawyers for Deng and her father replied, stating that the plaintiff's allegations were unfounded. If Fang Danchi really had hundreds of thousands of property, why didn't he say a word to his son before his death? If Deng had really committed theft, she would have fled and been afraid to be found, how could she have escorted the coffin back to her hometown and observed mourning? Finally, lawyer Jiang Yiping defended Wang Shutang. The court ordered that the verdict be announced on the morning of July 21.

After the soaring gold prices, the trams and buses in the Public Concession had already raised their prices. According to the Guowen News Agency, Bao Jusheng, a silk merchant from Huzhou, lived at Hengmao Silk Shop in Dean Lane, North Suzhou Road. At 9:50 pm on the 6th of this month, he finished bathing at Tianfa Pool on Nanjing Road and was returning home. Therefore, he has decided to prepare all the evidence and formally negotiate with the reporter.

Municipal Public Works Bureau Urges Gao Deli to Connect to Tap Water 170

Gao Deli Lane on Zhiyuan Road, Zhabei, has an artesian well for supplying drinking water to tenants. However, the well is too shallow, and the water quality is turbid. The tenants in the lane have asked the landlord to connect to tap water but have been refused. They reported this to the Municipal Public Works Bureau, which sent personnel to investigate and found that the well was equipped with two hand-operated pumps that were operated manually. Recently, due to the low water level, the pumps have failed, resulting in frequent water outages. The tenants have requested to connect to tap water, but the rental office is still hesitant because the well has been repaired several times and has cost a lot of money. After the Municipal Public Works Bureau sent personnel to earnestly persuade them, they entrusted the Tongli Water and Electricity Company to connect the water pipes. Now, they have formally reported to the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company to connect the water.

Huge Amount of Smuggled Opium Intercepted in the Huangpu River 172

Cases of river steamers smuggling opium into the port are often discovered. At about 7 pm the night before last (the 13th), someone on a certain foreign steamer from the Yangtze River smuggled a large amount of opium. Because the ship docked in Pudong, the smuggled opium was secretly loaded onto a small sampan while no one was paying attention and secretly unloaded from the ship. A certain person engaged in smuggling accompanied the opium across the river, intending to land at the Taikoo Company Wharf in the French Concession. At that time, the French Concession was holding a Democratic Republic Anniversary celebration, and the foreign firms along the Bund were decorated with electric lights, and French officials and gentry were holding lantern parades to celebrate. Spectators gathered, and the smugglers were trying to take advantage of the crowds to blend in. Unexpectedly, the police authorities had received a report early on and dispatched detectives and prepared a car to wait in front of the Taikoo Wharf. When the sampan arrived at the port, the detectives boarded the boat and searched it, seizing two large sacks and one large bag of smuggled opium on the spot, the quantity was very large. The person escorting the opium saw that the smuggled opium had been seized and jumped into the Huangpu River in an attempt to commit suicide, but he was pulled up by the detectives, he was half submerged. The smuggled opium was immediately loaded into a car and taken away. The escorting criminal was taken by small steamer to the east of the Qing Concession.

Old Woman Transporting Six Packages of Opium 173

At the South Railway Station of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway yesterday morning at about 8:00 am, the fourth express train to Hangzhou was about to depart. An old woman, about sixty years old, came to the station to buy a ticket to Chang'an. Detectives and soldiers stationed at the station by the Songhu Garrison Command, saw that the old woman looked suspicious and approached her. They discovered six packages of opium, weighing more than ninety taels, in the old woman's trunk. The person and the goods were detained. It is reported that the old woman's name is Jia Ding, sixty years old. The opium was entrusted to her by someone else, who paid her four yuan as a reward to transport it to Chang'an Station, where someone would receive it.

Abduction of an Underage Girl 174

Wang Lanyu, a Huizhou native who runs an ink-making shop in Chaguan Lane, Nancang Street, outside Xiaonanmen, has a daughter, Wang Lianshi, who is nineteen years old this year. She is petite, exquisite, and beautiful, and rarely leaves the house. However, Cao Liyi, a frivolous loafer employed by Wang, often seduced Lianshi, flattering her in every way. There was no good outcome for the single man and resentful woman. Until yesterday, Cao actually tricked Lianshi into going out. When they arrived at Xiaodongmenkou, Wang asked Lianshi to spend the rest of her life with him and go to Nanjing with him. However, Lianshi was thinking of her parents and could not bear to be separated, so she was unwilling to go with him. Cao then devised a plan to take her to the Bund Wharf, intending to trick her onto a ship and achieve his abduction. However, Wang, having learned that his daughter had gone out and also seeing that Cao was not there, knew that there must be something wrong, so he ordered his eldest son, Wang Zida, to go out and search for her. Therefore, Cao and the others were seen by Wang Zida while they were wandering around the wharf, and he twisted them up and dragged them home. Lianshi told her father about what had happened. Wang Lanyu immediately twisted up Cao and took him to the First District First Precinct, requesting an investigation. After questioning, Wang Lianshi confessed, "Cao Liyi did abduct me. I was unwilling." Cao Liyi confessed, "Lianshi and I loved each other and could not bear to be separated. She voluntarily went out with me in order to facilitate the freedom of marriage." The chief of the precinct, having heard the confessions, determined that the case involved the abduction of a girl under the age of twenty. Therefore, he transferred the case to the District Court for trial yesterday.

Female Switchboard Operator Dies from Opium Consumption 175

▲ In-laws thought she was suffering from heatstroke

▲ Sent to the hospital for treatment but could not be saved

Li Zhou, a female switchboard operator at the China Foreign Telephone Company, was a Cantonese woman aged twenty-five. At 7:30 am the day before yesterday, she went from her residence in the French Concession to visit her in-laws, Li Shuncai and Li Bai, at 513 Sandu Lane (Chinese Concession) on Jiaozhou Road, West Shanghai. After talking about family affairs for a short while, Li Zhou suddenly suffered from 河鱼之疾 (sudden severe pain), her abdomen ached severely, and her face turned pale. Her mother-in-law, Li Bai, thought it was heatstroke because it was the height of summer, so she urgently hired a car to take her to the Labor Hospital on Xiaoshadu Road for treatment. However, the illness was severe, and she died in the hospital at about 9 am. The hospital then reported to the Putuo Road Police Station, which sent detective Zhao Fuhai to investigate. According to the neighbors, Li Zhou's death was not from a disease, but from consuming opium. They took the body to the Ferron Road Forensic Examination Office. Yesterday morning, Xu, a prosecutor from the Special District Court, arrived at the office and confirmed that the deceased had indeed died from consuming opium. The court summoned Li Shuncai and his wife to give testimony. They testified, "When our daughter-in-law came, she showed no signs of anything unusual. Later, she complained of abdominal pain, and we suspected it was heatstroke, so we sent her to the hospital. We really don't know if she consumed opium." After the examination, Prosecutor Xu ordered Li Shuncai to sign a statement and claim the body for burial.

Kong Qingyu is Too Unprincipled 176

▲ Attempted to rape a friend's daughter

▲ Even dared to commit assault with a knife

Xu Yuhe, a salt merchant from Yancheng who is a road construction worker, lives in a bungalow behind the Xiangyan Bridge Fenshui Temple in Hujia Bridge. He had a friend named Kong Qingyu, who is fifty-nine years old this year and has no family. Xu took him in because he thought he had no one to take care of him. Unexpectedly, Kong was ungrateful. Recently, the weather has been hot, and Xu has an eighteen-year-old daughter, Xu Da'e. Da'e was taking a bath in the room. Kong, who was bored, wandered around and heard the sound of water in the room. He peeked through the crack in the door and saw Da'e bathing naked. Kong could not restrain himself and pushed the door open and grabbed her to rape her. Da'e screamed for help, and her grandmother, Gan Zhu, heard it. She stepped forward to pull Kong away and scolded him for being an animal. Kong was enraged and chopped Gan Zhu's head with a knife. Fortunately, the neighbors arrived and restrained Kong and called the police at the Fifth District Third Precinct. Yesterday, he was presented to the Public Security Bureau and transferred to the District Court for investigation and punishment.

Chen Aizhu Demands Marital Autonomy 177

Chen Aizhu, the adopted daughter of Chen Zhangsheng, is twenty-nine years old. Chen has no children, so he cherishes Aizhu. The marriage contract between Chen Aizhu and Chen Azhu was made in the 17th year of the Republic (1928) and wedding was planned for the autumn this year. Unexpectedly, Aizhu has recently changed her behavior, even leaving the family and staying outside. Yesterday morning, Judge Tong Shenglv continued the hearing. The plaintiff, Chen Aizhu, was absent. The defendant, Chen Azhu, testified that he made a marriage agreement with Aizhu on March 26 of the previous year and sent her forty yuan in gifts and four pieces of gold jewelry on that day. In September of last year, he sent another two hundred and eighty yuan as a wedding gift. They originally intended to marry in August of this year, and he requested that the marriage contract remain valid. Chen Zhangsheng testified that his adopted daughter, Aizhu, has been working as a seamstress. He now knows that his daughter has been hidden by Zhao Maotou, a worker at the Riyue Port Paper Mill. Chen Hu (Chen Zhangsheng's wife) testified that she had obtained Aizhu's consent when they made the marriage contract in the past. Unexpectedly, Aizhu was seduced by someone and fled outside on the third day of November of last year, leading to litigation. She requested that the court fulfill the marriage. Defendant's lawyer Liu Xiangqi also made a statement. The judge said that the plaintiff was not present today, but the plaintiff was not old enough, and she must have a guardian in order to be legal. He would send another summons, and if she was not present next time, the court would make a judgment.

▲ His wife has run away without a trace

The defendant, Jin Wang, was not present because her address was unknown and could not be served. A special agent, lawyer Zhou Yu, appeared in court to make a statement on her behalf. In the summer of last year, she was young (Jin Wang was 22 years old and from Suzhou) and was tricked by someone and committed adultery with him. Exposure of the Abduction of an Adopted Daughter 180

▲ The evil deeds of matchmakers

Jin Yukang, a thirty-nine-year-old man from Shaoxing, lives at number 120 in a lane on Haichao Temple Street outside Xiaonanmen. He is employed in a foreign goods store in Annam, so he is often away from home and rarely returns. His wife, Xiao, is thirty-four years old. Although they have been married for many years, they have no children, so they bought a girl named A Lin as an adopted daughter. A Lin is seventeen years old this year and is quite beautiful, but she is temperamental. Last month, Xiao suddenly gave birth to a son and was overjoyed. She hired a Songjiang woman, Yu Shen, as a wet nurse. More than a month later, Chen He, a woman from the same hometown as Shen, often came to chat. After seeing A Lin, she suddenly became tempted to abduct her. So she used her skills to seduce A Lin, who fell into her trap. At about 11 am yesterday, Xiao was about to cook lunch and ordered her daughter to take a pot to fetch water. After leaving, she met He and was invited into a small lane to talk. Chen He said, "You are suffering here. Why don't you go back to Songjiang with me? Then you won't have to worry about clothing and food. If you are willing, I will wait at the Guanqiao Wharf now, and you can come quickly. Then we can go together. I have all the money, so don't worry." A Lin was moved by vanity and agreed. Xiao was at home, waiting for a long time and did not see A Lin return. Anxiously, she went out to look for her and happened to see A Lin talking quietly with He in a small lane. Suspicious, she stepped forward and questioned them. He saw that she had been exposed and fled. Xiao scolded A Lin and ordered her to fetch water. After lunch, A Lin suddenly disappeared without a trace. Xiao was convinced that she had been abducted by He. She remembered that He was acquainted with the wet nurse Shen and detained Shen. She went to the matchmaker's shop on Nancang Street to investigate. The matchmaker's shop, because it was responsible, immediately sent people out to search for her. At about 3 pm, they found A Lin waiting for a boat with He at the Guanqiao Wharf. They immediately took them to Haichao Temple Street and reported to Zhang Wenjin, the watchman of the twenty-sixth post in that area, and brought them back to the First District Third Precinct. Jin, the precinct chief, presented the case for a preliminary hearing. Because the case involved the abduction of a young girl, he ordered that a document be prepared and sent to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation.
