The Detention of Hu Yingyi for Using Counterfeit Money for One Year 185

▲ Hu's Request for Redemption Denied

Hu Yingyi, a 25-year-old from Guangdong, went to the An Le Palace dance hall on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession on the evening of April 24th this year to drink and dance with the dance hostesses several times. He paid with a Hong Kong bank note worth 100 yuan, equivalent to 14 silver dollars, instructing them to find him 86 silver dollars in change. The hall owner discovered that the note was counterfeit. He later learned that Hu was hiding in the Da Dong Hotel in the International Settlement. He immediately reported this to the French police station, which sent detectives to arrest him. It turned out that the defendant had also committed a similar offense of using counterfeit money in the International Settlement and had been arrested by detectives and brought before the Special District Court. After interrogation, he was sentenced to two and a half years of imprisonment and fined 1,400 yuan. A few days ago, detectives from the French police station went to bring Hu before the French court. First, the manager of An Le Palace, Zhang Xingfa, recounted the previous events. When questioned, Hu Yingyi confessed that the counterfeit banknote was obtained when he sold a ring to a civilian in Hong Kong for 400 yuan. He claimed he had not dared to counterfeit it himself and that he was dissatisfied with the sentence imposed by the Special District Court and had filed an appeal. After hearing the case, the Chinese and Western judges determined that the defendant had indeed used counterfeit money and sentenced him to one year in the Western prison as a warning to others. The defendant requested to be allowed to pay a fine to avoid imprisonment, but the court rejected his request.

Expansion of the California Oil Company 187

The California Oil Company, one of the major oil companies in the United States, has recently dispatched representatives to China to conduct a thorough preliminary investigation to expand its operations and compete with existing companies such as Standard Oil, Asiatic Petroleum, and Texaco. The representatives arrived in Shanghai a few days ago on the President Madison of the Dollar Line. They had previously visited Hong Kong to conduct a detailed examination. It is expected that their survey in China will take at least six months to complete. The California Oil Company has a capital of US$125 million and is headquartered in Los Angeles, California. It is one of the largest companies on the Pacific coast producing and selling petroleum products. It has extensive oil fields in the southern and central United States, Mexico, and Venezuela, and seven oil refineries. Its products include kerosene, gasoline, machine oil, and paving asphalt. It has been selling in China for many years, but on a small scale. This time, it plans to expand significantly and join the competition.

Art World

Peasant Art 191

Written by Yamamoto Kanae, translated by Chen Baoyi (Part 1)

Regarding peasant art (L’Art Rustique), although some books have been published on it in England, France, Germany, Russia, Italy, etc., there does not seem to be a comprehensive historical account like those of general art. It is mostly introduced from the perspective of folklore research or industrial inspection.

According to anthropological research, the origins of peasant art date back to the eleventh and twelfth centuries. It was significantly developed among the rural villagers in northern Sweden, which was once the cultural center of the ancient Western Hemisphere (see Adachi's "Swedish Peasant Art"). Although it is generally referred to as peasant art, it is not limited to peasants but also found among fishermen and herders. However, the wood carvings and inlaid woodwork made by herders in the Austrian Highlands are called L’Art Pastoral (shepherd art) by folklore researchers. In short, wherever people lived in the past, there was some form of peasant art. In ancient times, all necessities of life were self-sufficient. Before there were specialized workers or shops, household utensils and ornaments were made by everyone themselves. Even today, in remote and secluded places similar to ancient times, everything is still self-sufficient. For example, in our country (Japan), the indigenous areas of Taiwan are like this. Originally, since they became Japanese citizens and goods could be bought with money, their L’Art Rustique has almost disappeared. However, even now, the houses they live in, such as the main pillars of the houses, the ancestral images used in ceremonies, the beautiful clothes worn during rituals, the weapons with relief carvings on the sheaths and handles, the wine cups shared by two people, the bamboo harmonicas, the rattan hats, and the unglazed water jars, are all works of the indigenous villages. We call these self-made crafts "self-use crafts" in classification.

In the past, all peasant art was self-use craft. Although it cannot be said that everything was made by the user's own hands, it generally refers to the decorative crafts made in the countryside by individuals, families, villages, or local communities for their own use. It seems appropriate to call this L’Art Rustique. Among this kind of peasant art, Scandinavia is the richest in examples. For example, large tapestries woven with stripes or patterns, large furniture with relief carvings of vine-like patterns, and beautiful mats and vests embroidered with flowers are all exquisite and unique.

The first impression of the characteristic peasant art of Switzerland can be felt from the architecture. The farmhouses (Chalet or Dwellings) in the Alps often have round stones on their roofs, and the eaves, windows, and cabinets are decorated with relief carvings. The characteristic of Switzerland is mostly woodwork and wood carvings, such as wardrobes, cradles, snow sleds, chairs, and wooden clocks. These are all complete works of art and craft. Herders who live far from people in the mountains probably still make their own supplies like the ancients.

A book records... (Herders are not just herdsmen, but also craftsmen, carpenters, and artists. They do not hold pens, but rather knives as artists, creators, and Altists, especially sculptors. Pens and paper are not their tools, but knives are always with them. They use knives to carve their imaginations onto pieces of Swiss pine or larch wood. Human figures, wild or domestic livestock, and other creatures, flowers and plants are natural and natural models for them.) Gold and silver thread embroidery and hand-woven fabrics are famous peasant arts of Belgium and the joyful work of mountain village women during the winter.

[When snow falls and strong winds blow for one or two weeks continuously, there are desolate cold nights. Heavy snow prevents the traces of pedestrians and buries beautiful villages in all white. Inside the house, homemade dried cheese is placed on a handmade tablecloth. After a happy family dinner, the women cheerfully take out spindles and spinning wheels on long cold nights, take out needle sticks for making lace from small boxes with relief carvings, or spread out embroidery tools under the lamp, or sit at the loom by the window. The well-used shuttles, passed down from grandmothers in ancient times, are used to weave threads with momentum.

Look, the loom goes *thump thump karari*

The maiden making a living is *happy even in her expression*

The sounds of songs being sung as they work leak out from each household, || and during the summer, patterns copied from grass and trees are unfolded,

and colored threads are traced on beautiful cloth.

In such a cold winter scene, their decorative crafts are thus completed.

Italian peasant art was also once prosperous. Chiseled gold and silver filigree with painted patterns, unglazed pottery with blue and yellow colors, embroidery lace, hand-woven fabrics, and woodwork are quite rich.

Even in Germany, peasant art was once widespread. It is described in German books as follows:

From the external decoration of houses to the smallest decorations in clothing, but belonging to rural crafts, interior decoration furniture, utensils, kiln products, metal handicrafts, decorative clothing, temple supplies, and the walls around cemeteries, gardens, and houses, that is, all these techniques of carving, inlaying, stonemasonry, painting, pottery, weaving, embroidery, machine weaving, blacksmithing, and filigree of precious metals are included. These products are the result of hard work during the winter and are mostly made by rural artisans.

Even in France, Austria, and Hungary, peasant art was once prosperous. France is known for its lace and white thread embroidery, while Austria and Hungary are known for their wood crafts with inlaid metal fittings, and wool-woven brocade tapestries or tablecloths. In short, in the same era, roughly the same peasant art was practiced in all other European countries. Where did the rural villagers of the time learn their designs and techniques? Mainly from temple art. Therefore, this peasant art method has Gothic or Byzantine styles, and their farmers have simple tastes and honest methods. Unknowingly, it has created a simple and profound style. As for taking the delicate Louis style as important, being tired of the strong quirks of the new art, and gradually feeling dissatisfied with the unstable geometric Secession (Note A) || Europe's recent art world, on its path to regeneration, can afford to pay attention to the peasant art of the past. It is a big, understandable matter.

(Note A: Secession, which began in 1897)

(A new style in Austria that separated from traditional classical art)

With the spread of stores and the rise of factories, and with the end of the era of self-sufficiency, peasant art also almost disappeared. Like the end of the Warring States period, spears and swords became antiques. Peasant art, which was once a favorite item of rural villagers, also became an antique and was transported from the countryside to collection halls or scholars and artists. Today, it is impossible to see the above-mentioned self-use crafts in farmhouses. The peasant art made today is not for personal use, but for sale, just like the vegetables or fruits made by farmers to meet the needs of the city. However, it is an industry. Therefore, peasant art like today is, first of all, unnecessary and unharmonious in the lives of the farmers who make it, but the authors can earn money from those products and also enjoy their art work. However, this is exactly the opposite of the peasant art of the past. The peasant art of the past was intimately harmonized with the author's environment and was probably a cherished object that they did not want to exchange for money. Here we can divide peasant art into two types: ||

A. Peasant art for self-use craft (most of the peasant art in ancient times belonged to this type)

B. Peasant art for industrial craft (most of the peasant art today belongs to this type)

In short, with the modern economic situation, A has disappeared and B has risen. The rise of B and the fact that it is being encouraged in various countries have two legitimate reasons: first, to attach importance to peasant art from the standpoint of folk education in the face of the desolation of rural life today; and second, to focus interest on its development as a reflection of urban taste and mechanical production. Dr. Chonglai, the chairman of the Rural Welfare and Local Customs Association in Germany, once said (handicrafts and craft skills were accompanied by self-use crafts everywhere in the countryside, fulfilling its

Turkish children learning new alphabets

astonishing development. Household utensils, implements, and everything were made and repaired by farmers with knives, chisels, hammers, and saws, to a certain extent artistically, practically, sturdily, and with a unique charm. Thus, even during the winter, farmers, families, servants, and laborers all had sufficient work, and the work rooms of each farmer became a place for implementing manual education. Today, the carvings, metalwork, machine weaving, embroidery, and other works of art from peasant hands that are displayed in many museums are made by the rough hands of farmers engaged in threshing, feeding livestock, or cultivating the land. Those unique crafts or utensils can now hardly be seen in farmhouses. The things that farmers used to make themselves in their homes during the winter off-season must now be bought from factories. Factory products are cheaper, but their durability is far inferior to the manual work of farmers in their free time. If it is only a question of how to obtain such utensils in the easiest and cheapest way, then we probably would not express any different opinions regarding this change. However, the problem is much more serious. Along with the decline of self-use crafts and handicrafts, the character of the local people has lost one of its most solid characteristics. Taste education and extremely unique artistic ideas have disappeared or degenerated. Practical skills and adaptability to all manual operations have become increasingly weakened. We must be aware of this matter as a folk education problem. Why? It is because, due to the increasing development of mechanical industry, most of the winter labor of the local people has been encroached upon, and the leisure time that should be used for manual work is far more than in the past. Therefore, in folk education, we always demand that the self-use crafts and other manual skills that were once popular, which have now disappeared, be revived through manual education under a certain direction.)

Submission Guidelines for the Art World 192

(1) Articles should be limited to news, reviews, and introductions related to the latest art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature at home and abroad.

(2) Pictures should be limited to recent works by new domestic and foreign artists and accompanying illustrations related to the text.

(3) Photos should be limited to recent portraits and works of domestic and foreign artists and various photographs related to the text.

(4) Each article should not exceed 3,000 words.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, and avoid sloppy handwriting. Western languages should be minimized. If it is absolutely necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

Social News

New Uses for Wood Flour 193

Wood flour was used in Germany during the European War, but many people still consider it unreliable and insufficient to replace other materials. However, in many places in the United States, it is gradually being used for flooring, shelves, and wall coatings, and wood flour has become an industry. The United States has a history of forty years, with an average annual output of more than 24,000 tons. The Scandinavian countries and Germany produce 6,000 tons of sales in the Atlantic coast of the United States each year. The main uses are mostly in the manufacture of stoppers, rubber, and tarpaulins. Even for statues, New York uses 5,000 tons each year. More than 75% of these wood flours in the United States are from white pine sawing, and the rest are mostly from poplar, palm, alder wood and maple wood. Now because of the high cost of sawing, the high cost is not easy to transport. The inconvenience is being engaged in improvement. This kind of wood sawing in China is equal to waste wood flour in the United States, but it has become a major industry, and it is felt that the Chinese are doing foolish things when sawing wood, throwing away hundreds of items on the ground. It is hoped that someone will pay attention to the use of this waste, which will also provide a small subsidy to the national economy. (Yi Kang)

The Future of Radio News Transmission 194

Currently, the San Francisco Daily News in the United States has been read by the New York Total Electric Company by machine three hours after publication. In the future, what can be transmitted is a 38-inch strip, which can be transmitted by radio. Other radio photographs can also be transmitted at the same time. However, the San Francisco Daily News obtained by radio transmission is not the original form, but an 8-inch rolled paper printed by the radio company. This 8-inch rolled paper is printed by a machine that can print half an inch per minute. The entire contents of the San Francisco Daily News can be read on the 8-inch rolled paper in about four minutes. This rolled paper is specially made into a rolled type for printing (Yi Kang)

Italy to Build Magnificent Giant Ships 195

The Italian government has decided to build a giant and beautiful Mediterranean ship like a palace, as other countries have gorgeous and spectacular ships, and Italy is in urgent need of this equipment. In addition to ordinary equipment, there will be churches, swimming pools, sports grounds, theaters, and airports. It is planned to be 887 feet long, 97 feet wide, weighing 45,000 tons, and the horsepower will be increased to 90,000 horsepower, traveling at 27 nautical miles per hour. The people living on the ship must be people on the Italian coastline, and each room will have a wireless telephone to communicate with each other. This plan has been actively implemented by the government and is expected to be successful next year. (Yi Kang)

Research on Radio Transmission from the Moon 196

Radio in the United States has made great progress thanks to the efforts of researchers. However, there is still no practical evidence for the experiment of broadcasting radio signals to the moon. However, Dr. A. Hoyt Taylor, fleet radio engineer of the Naval Experimental Chemical Laboratory, has spent a long time researching this experiment. The doctor hopes that the moon's surface can reflect a signal to the ground when the moon is only 250,000 miles from the earth. It is expected that the specially set Hertzian wave can travel 186,000 miles per second. In two and a half seconds, the signal reflected by the surface of the moon can be received in Washington. The doctor is currently researching this matter. The radio industry believes that the success of this experiment will open a new era, because radio recently broadcast from New York to Celle, Austria, and the reflection reply was obtained in a short period of time. (Yi Kang)

Car King's Profit Last Year 197

The cars of the American Ford Motor Company have been sold throughout the country. Since the development of sales markets in Northern and Eastern Europe last year, the business has increased sharply. Recently, the Chicago newspaper in the United States declared that the profit for 1929 was quite surprising. The net profit for this year was US$81,797,861, an increase of more than 10 million yuan compared with 42 million yuan in 1927 and 72 million yuan in 1928. (Yi Kang)

(2) Pictures should be limited to various lyrical paintings about social life.

Group News 199

▲ The Municipal National Arts Museum announced that the museum's Taijiquan special class has been established for a year, and a large number of members have joined. A few days ago, the venue director, Mr. Ye Liang, initiated a gathering at the Great China Restaurant to connect with each other. More than 30 people, including Professor Wu Jianquan, venue director Mr. Ye Liang, and male and female members, attended. For a time, the guests clinked glasses, talked and laughed, and dispersed at about 10 o'clock.

Business News 200

▲ The Franco-Chinese Pharmacy announces that this year's "Double Lion" brand mosquito incense, a domestic product, has been produced with even greater improvements than in previous years. All materials and decoration have also been improved. As a result, sales are consistently strong both locally and in other regions. The factory's products are in high demand, with supply often falling short of demand. Each box comes with a metal burning tray; once lit, mosquitoes will die and users can sleep soundly without worry.

▲ Maochang Optical Company on Mintuan Road, west of the Old North Gate, announces that since the establishment of their low-price department, the store has been bustling with customers. Their optical fittings are precise, and those who require myopia glasses have been universally full of praise. In order to make their products accessible to all, they have not raised prices and still sell each pair for one yuan.

▲ Daguan Bookstore, located at 210 Fangxie Road, Ximen (West Gate), is a bookstore specializing in literary and party-oriented books. After a month of preparation, it has officially commenced business on the 10th (the day before yesterday). On that day, there were many guests and the female staff provided attentive service. Currently, during the initial opening period, the prices of all books are particularly affordable. They sincerely welcome patronage from all walks of life. It is reported that the official grand opening will be held in the autumn when schools resume.

▲ The Sino-Western Pharmacy main store on Fourth Road announces that, given the recent hot weather and prevalence of epidemics, they are offering various summer epidemic prevention drugs at particularly low prices for two weeks. There will also be various free gifts, such as fans, perfumes, gift vouchers, and tickets to the Great World amusement park. In the eyes of customers, when spending money to buy goods, naturally those who can get free gifts will be preferred. Therefore, the pharmacy has been crowded with customers for days, and the staff is busy, with supply often falling short of demand. Especially at sunset, the number of customers is even greater. It is reported that in these two or three days, the sales of Epidemic Prevention Water, Merit, and Water Brandy amount to more than 27,000 boxes per day.

▲ Yanhua Restaurant, opposite the Dangui No. 1 Stage on Fourth Road, announces that their cold drink section is well-equipped and has ample ventilation. Electric fans are installed everywhere, so even in hot weather, one does not feel the heat. Therefore, recently, people from all walks of life have been flocking to enjoy cold drinks and light refreshments, especially those from foreign firms and banks. The cold drink section has recently added ice cream sodas, which are priced at only 25 cents per glass. All flavors of ice cream are sold for 16 cents per serving. The cold drink section has recently been expanded and various shaved ice products are planned to be added. The renovation has been completed and these products will soon be available.

▲ Qingyise Restaurant, at the intersection of Third Road and Zhejiang Road, announces that their seasonal vegetarian dishes are numerous and varied. Among the most delicious are Three Shredded Dishes with Black Moss, Braised Mushrooms with Loofah, Dried Mushrooms with Straw Mushrooms and Salted Bean Curd, Gluten and Dew Bamboo Shoots, and Straw Mushrooms with Gluten. They are clean, not greasy, and exquisitely prepared, with very low prices. Therefore, recently, more people than before have been coming for vegetarian meals. The vegetarian chef is under contract for only two months and will no longer cook after the contract expires.

▲ Hanli Company announces that their newly invented Zhongling pneumatic printing press, from the beginning, was priced extremely low in order to make it accessible to all and facilitate printing. Recently, the price of gold has skyrocketed and all goods have become more expensive. All industries have announced price increases. However, Zhongling Printing Machine wants to maintain its reputation as a domestic product and defeat foreign goods, so it would rather suffer losses itself and dare not raise prices. At a time when the scorching heat prevails, and there are many documents in the military, government, commercial, and academic sectors, every stroke of the pen causes sweat to flow down the back. If the Zhongling Military is used, tens of thousands of papers can be completed in an instant, and they are unusually clear. What a refreshing and convenient way to save time and money! No wonder everyone is happy to buy it. Furthermore, since the company posted advertisements to recruit provincial managers, within three days, major stores in Guizhou, Sichuan, and Liaoning provinces have ordered managers and shipped back large quantities of printing machines to promote sales within their provincial areas.

▲ Zhonghua Enamel Factory announces that they have added a Penglai retail store to facilitate retail customers and revitalize the South City market. All Lihe brand basins, food baskets, tea trays, cups, and all household utensils are sold at wholesale prices. They also accept orders for various ceramic signs such as door numbers, license plates, and shop signs. Since the opening, business has been very lively. Because the weather is very hot, the reception is considered inadequate, so they have extended the evening hours until 9:30 PM to better serve customers.

▲ Shanghai Film Company announces that their "Pansi Cave" play has already caused a sensation in society. After the sequel to "Pansi Cave" was screened, it was packed every day and latecomers could not find a place. Therefore, there were many who regretted missing it. Therefore, from the 19th of this month, the Zhengxu "Pansi Cave," two major films, will be screened together at the Central Grand Theater. It is a rare opportunity.

▲ Xifan Film Company announces that after the completion of the two new films "Four Heroes of Affection" and "Heroine in Rouge," they are now preparing to produce a great drama "Golden Rooster Ridge." The drama is a martial arts story of sword immortals of the Qing Dynasty.

▲ Tongle Amusement Park announces that this park is organized by Zeng Junbaoquan. The interior decorations are artistic and the various entertainment acts are selected from the best in Shanghai. When Mr. Zeng was in charge of the New New Amusement Park, his performance was remarkable. Mr. Zeng originally was, so the internal arrangements of this Tongle Amusement Park are very impressive. All the entertainment of an amusement park has been collected, such as Peking Opera, New Opera, makeup, Suzhou Beach Circus, dance troupe, storytelling hall, dance hall, magic, etc. There is also a cold drink area for tourists to cool off and escape the summer heat. It is currently being decorated day and night and will open soon. The location is at the original site of the Nanjing Road Municipal Government.

▲ Paris Grand Theater announces that starting yesterday, the theater will screen the latest masterpiece "The Love of a Slave," co-starring America's top beauty (Ben Hur) leading man Ramon Novarro and (Cossack) leading actress Renee Adoree. The plot of the film tells the story of a romantic emperor who, because of his love for a woman, would rather sacrifice his throne and flee with the woman to another place. It is a fragrant and romantic story, and can be called the supreme masterpiece of silent films.

▲ Fanwang Palace Cinema on Shengmuyuan Road and Tongfu Road in West Shanghai announces that, due to its perfect facilities, fresh air, and low prices and excellent films, the theater has been sold out every day since its opening. In order to give preferential treatment to the audience, starting today, in addition to the famous film "Glittering Night Life," they have specially invited a famous and beautiful Russian dancer to perform mysterious dances that have never been seen in Shanghai. Ticket prices remain at 20 cents and 40 cents.

Medical News 202

Dr. Ma Jemei, at 52 Songshan Road, is proficient in qihuang and especially good at injections. He treats various departments of men, women, and children, as well as all kinds of miscellaneous diseases, and he always succeeds in bringing patients back to health. Patients from far and near have praised him. Those seeking medical attention are constantly busy. Yesterday afternoon, the wife of Qian Jiufu, the director of the Second District and First Office of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, suddenly suffered from dry cholera. Her limbs were already cold and her condition was extremely dangerous. Dr. Ma Jemei was rushed to the rescue. He first performed surgery and then administered medicine, and she was able to turn the crisis into safety.

▲ Dr. Yan Cangshan, a famous doctor in Shanghai, is the founder of the Family Medicine Advisory Society. His academic experience has long been well-known in society. Last winter, the wife of Cen Qisheng, a pharmaceutical giant, had a miscarriage and was in critical condition. Dr. Yan cured her. Mr. Cen was grateful and asked Wang Yiting to inscribe the four characters "Recreating Great Kindness" on a plaque, which was delivered to Dr. Yan's clinic at 420 Pubo Road in the French Concession yesterday. The scene was quite lively for a while.
